Family Council
For over ten years, FAMILY COUNCIL has
provided innovative Family Education programs
involving all facets of the congregation. Several
large scale projects like Rabbi Dov Kentof’s
Fantasy Noah’s Ark , Sukkah Decorating and
Hanukkah Activity Day inspire the entire
congregation including the Center Preschool,
Solomon Schechter Day School, Afternoon
Hebrew School and Sunday School. Synagogue
professionals, volunteer experts, parents and
children provide valuable input and assistance and
are rewarded by the experience.

Religious Schools
Afternoon Hebrew School
The Afternoon Hebrew School of the Jacksonville Jewish Center is designed for students in grades 3-7, and provides an
elementary education leading to Bar/Bat Mitzvah and continuation in the high school program.
Meeting on Mondays, Wednesdays and Saturdays, “the basics” are at the core of the curriculum, with stress on Hebrew
reading, Jewish social studies, and current events relating to Israel. Synagogue skills, holiday observances and knowledge of
prayers are all part of the comprehensive Afternoon Hebrew School program.

Confirmation
Celebrated 6 & 7 Sivan 5759 • May 20 -21, 1999
The Biblical festival of Shavuot commemorates the giving of the Torah and Ten Commandments to the
Jewish people. It is natural that this festival should be celebrated with an accompanying sense of commitment to
Jewish life that Confirmation represents. Confirmands demonstrate the knowledge gained through the completion
of our Hebrew High program by full participation in Shavuot services.

Beit Midrash
Jacksonville Community Hebrew High School
Pamela Maman - Director
The Center’s 8th through 11th grades participate in the community
Hebrew High School program. The following courses will be taught this
year: Jewish Belief, Israeli Geography, Jewish Life in Literature, L’Dor
Y’Dor - Generation to Generation, Introduction to Conversational
Hebrew, Hassidic Tales of the Holocaust, Judaism in Word and Deed,
The Jewish Book of Why, and Advanced Hebrew.

Center Youth Groups
Research has proven that the survival of Judaism depends on the exposure of our youth to Jewish activities, friends and
experiences that commit them to perpetuating that feeling of Jewishness and Jewish life.
The Jacksonville Jewish Center sponsors three outstanding youth groups for youngsters in grades 4-12. Each group meets
regularly and enjoys programs of a religious, cultural and social nature.
Through active participation in these groups, a sense of pride and an identification with
Judaism are instilled. Jewish values, attitude and behavior patterns are discussed and carried out
through Mitzvah programs and study.
Conventions, regional activities and camps give our youth the opportunity to meet other
Jewish youth from all over the United States.
The youth programs are coordinated by Rabbi Dov Kentof, and are supervised by the
Youth Commission. All groups are affiliated with the Southeast Region and United Synagogue of
America.

Youth Activities
Summer Programs for Jewish Youth
Camp Ramah Palmer and Ramah Darom
The Jacksonville Jewish Center is very fortunate to have a large representation
of youngsters participating in the Camp Ramah programs both in New England and
the new Ramah Darom in Georgia. Ramah, an arm of the Conservative Movement,
offers a wonderful summer opportunity for informal enrichment and meaningful
education.
Ashley Osterer (2nd row, 3-L) and Ramah friends.
Attending Camp Ramah Palmer in New England were: Ashley Osterer,
Amy Schuster and Shayna Weiss
U.S.Y. on Wheels
This fine program gives teenagers
an opportunity to travel around the
United States seeing landmarks,
historical sites and National parks. In
addition they meet Jewish youth in the
cities in which they stay. This year
Lauren Bloom, Crista Cohen, Rachel
Gerber, Sara Mizrahi, Aliza Morris,
Melissa Osterer, Lisa Rand, Rachel
Rosner, Jonathan Tannen and Jacob
Zoske joined other U.S.Y.ers on Wheels.

USY Israel/Poland Pilgrimage and Ramah in Israel
This is a unique opportunity for young people ages 15 to 18 to visit Israel. Based in Jerusalem each of our groups travels
the country experiencing their Jewish heritage. In addition to spending a delightful summer with their Israeli counterparts, our
“pilgrims” also develop lifelong friendships with their traveling companions from the United States and Canada. An additional
tour of Poland gives a deeper understanding of the Holocaust. Center US Yers who went on Pilgrimage were Josh Bernard,
Adele Blum, Mitchell Eaglstein, Aaron Finck, Ellen Goldstein, Sara Sekine, Drew Shenkman, Dani Spriggs, Blair Schemer,
Mindy Yergin and Esther Yegelwel. Jessica Osterer attended Ramah /Israel and an Eastern Europe Seminar.

Youth Activities
White Water Rafting Experience
Led by Rabbi Dov Kentof
LTI
Leadership Training Institute
Summer Encampment 1999
As always, this year’s White Water Rafting Trip was FANTASTIC! As in the
past, two rivers were explored: the Nolichucky and the French Broad. Everyone
had a blast, and made it home with all their body parts intact!
In addition, participants camped, held discussion groups, went tubing and
prayed in beautiful country settings. The memories made on this trip will last a
lifetime, and strengthen Judaism for these participants, in a unique way.
The trip was successful because of the help of Ava Axelrod, Rachel
Abramson, Dr. Michael Bernhardt, Philip Bloom, Joy & Mel Gottlieb, Alina
Kentof, Russell Selevan, Morris Shriftman, Lauren Snyder, Wesley Wallace,
Elliot Zisser and of course the participants. Special thanks to Laurie Schoettler
for putting together some great food!
Summers are topped off with a
unique one-week experience held each
August. This year, Ramah Darom was
the host camp. Teenagers participate in
programs that include informal classes
and discussion groups, cultural activities
and special evening activities in addition
to a full range of camp sports and social
activities. The camp provides two
unique programs: Kadima, grade 6, 7
& 8, and USY, grades 9 through 12.
Those attending were: Alexandra
Abramson, Dorie Bloom, Megan
Cohen and Erin Frisch.
Center Youth Banquet
May 16,1999
At the conclusion of the activity year, the Youth Commission holds a banquet
to honor the officers, advisors and volunteers from each Center Youth Group. Newly
elected officers for the coming year are introduced. This year’s banquet was made
even lovelier by the honoring of Rabbi Dov Kentof in a special program called
“Touched by Dov.” (See page 43 for details.)
Top: Advisor Karen Dubin installs
Chalutzim officers.
Above: USYers perform a traditional cheer.
Left: A record number of families and
friends attended the youth banquet.

Scouting
Daisy Troop 258
Daisy Girl Scout Troop 258 had a wonderful and fulfilling year! We formed new friendships that we hope will
last a lifetime. Through our weekly, fun-filled meetings, exciting field trips and inspiring ceremonies, these girls
have grown and blossomed before our eyes. The goals set from the Girl Scouts of America program were easily
achieved by these caring, sharing and ambitious young girls. We are very proud of them all. We truly enjoyed
sharing their experiences, and hope they will continue on as Brownies.
For more information call Laura Cagan, 260-9890, or Debbie Parker, 268-4339.
— Laura and Debbie
Brownie Troop 882
Brownie Troop 882 had a wonderful and busy year. Our girls were
involved in making the Hanukkah holiday bright for the residents at River
Garden. Besides creating beautiful stained glass vases and filling them full of
fresh flowers, the troop sang many of their favorite Hanukkah songs.
Our troop participated in gathering clothing and toys for the needy families
of Jacksonville. Each girl received a special patch for “Goodwill in our
Community.”
They learned about each; then they
related to them and their families.
During this year, the girls worked on many different “tryits”: animal,
creative composing, dancerize, good food, puppet, doll and plays, and safety,
either wrote or discussed the different topics, explaining how, as Girl Scouts, it
We also participated in the annual Girl Scout Cookie Sale. Our troop sold 1,500 boxes of cookies, which is the
all time high. Our troop also donated boxes of cookies to the Mandarin Food Bank, and received a patch for
Community Service.
This year, Troop #882 also donated a State Flag of Florida to the Solomon Schechter Day School. The older
Brownies of our troop presented the flag to Mr. Willard Kennedy, principal of the school.
Last but not least, our troop braved 30° weather to sleep in tents at the Girl Scout camp, Camp Chowenwaw.
The girls enjoyed a roaring campfire, and plenty of “sommores”. We walked along the shoreline of Black Creek,
sang songs and had a great weekend!
As Troop #882 grows and we welcome
a new bunch of brownies, we encourage any
parent willing to help with our larger troop
to contact either Beverly Eagerton, 880-
7525, or Lynn Kluger, 221-5748.
Brownies presenting flag to Mr.
Kennedy.
It has been a great year and we look
forward to our next year as leaders.
— Beverly and Lynn

===== PAGE 137 =====
Scouting
Junior Girl Scout Troop 5
Junior Troop 5 had a great year with 25 girls enjoying
scouting activities, and sharing their experiences and
adventures in Girl Scouting with younger girls!
This year our goal was to earn the “Sign of the Rainbow.”
This sign explores the five worlds of interest in Girl Scouting:
•The World of People — “Around the World” badge.
We saw a video about events from 1921 and tried on scout
uniforms from years past.
•The World of the Out-of-Doors —“Horse Lovers”
badge. As you can expect, we went horseback riding and
learned how to care for horses. At the Lake-Man-Jose
neighborhood Spring campout, the troop also earned the
“Finding Your Way” badge. This badge taught how to use a
compass, protractor, draw a map, and read a map. Good skills
for anyone to have!
•The World of Today and Tomorrow —’’Puzzlers” badge.
What fun it was to come to meetings and play board games!
•The World of the Arts —“Ceramics and Clay” badge.
The girls made pots and painted tiles to bring home and enjoy.
•The World of Well-Being —“Sports Sampler” badge.
Activities included a trip to the YMCA to learn tennis, a visit
from a Middle School coach, and a visit from a nurse to learn safety
and first aid in sports.
Girl Scouting is not only about learning and having fun
for ourselves, we also give back to the community as good
citizens. Toiletry bags were made and distributed to a local
homeless shelter. Our Girl Scout Cookie sale was a big success
(Who doesn’t love Girl Scout Cookies!) which we shared by
donating three cases of cookies to the Food Bank. Our girls
taught Brownie Troop # 882 about scouting, at a birthday
celebration for the founder of Girl Scouting, Juliette Gordon
Lowe. We also shared our Jewish heritage, and learned about
others, by visiting with Junior Troop #218, from St. Stephens
Church.
One of our scouts, Sarah Anderson, was selected for
the Gateway Council’s 6th grade event about Historic St.
Augustine in the 1740’s. She was a guide and teacher to tourists.
Thanks to Janis Fleet and Susan Cohen for serving as
Cookie Moms. Thanks also to Barbara Hunter, Badge Mom
for keeping our records straight, Jill Tager for her help when
we needed it, as well as all the other parents for their wonderful
support of their daughters and Troop 5!
—Helen Shacter and Shirley Jernigan
Cadette/Senior Girl Scout Troop 969
The troop kicked off the year with a camping weekend,
sleeping in tree houses, cooking, hiking and planning activities
that will carry us also through this coming year, The girls were
additionally able to share their Bat Mitzvah and Jewish holiday
experiences with a troop of girls from many other faiths. What
a wonderful experience for all of us in the woods by moonlight
under the stars! Other camp outs followed. Several Cadettes
helped Junior Girl Scouts learn compass skills and
orienteering, and several attended a council-wide Cadette-
Senior Weekend.
Cadette Troop 969 welcomed ten new members this
year! We also “bridged” two girls to Senior Girl Scouts, after
completion of their Silver projects. The Silver award is the,
second highest award in Girl Scouting and is earned at the
Cadette level. Lisa Rand and Crista Cohen completed their
work, a combination of interest patch achievement, service
and leadership, by teaching JJC Boy Scouts first aid
techniques. Congratulations girls!
Girl Scouts participated in several service projects: they
helped kick-off the Baptist/St. Vincent’s Health System-United
Way campaign by serving as greeters, serving refreshments
and manning a booth at a rally at the JCA, and participated in
a Good Will clothing drive. Crista also gave the invocation at
the National Conference honoring local Christian and Jewish
youth who had earned their religious awards in Boy and Girl
Scouting. Crista spoke on what the Menorah award (the
religious award for Jewish Girl Scouts) meant to her.
Girl Scouting affords friendship, fun, learning and
leadership opportunities for girls! We hope you will join us!
Girls in grades 7-12 are invited to participate in the
Jacksonville Jewish Center’s first Cadette/Senior Girl Scout
troop. Contact Karen Southall, leader, at 292-1337 or Jan
Lipsky, co-leader, at 268-7225.
Junior Girls Scout Troop 5 had a great time earning their badges

===== PAGE 139 =====
Scouting
Cub Scout Pack 14
Pack 14 recorded yet another outstanding year due to
the enthusiasm of a record 51 Cub Scouts and to our
exceptional den leaders. Some of our activities included the
annual Pinewood Derby competition at River Garden, camping
and winning many awards at the Riverbend District Cub-o-ree
campout, our Memorial Day camp out, learning outdoor skills,
and making Hanukkah gifts for sick individuals at Wolfson
Children’s Hospital.
The Blue and Gold Banquet recognized all the awards
and achievements our Cub and Boy Scouts had earned during
the past year. Special thanks to Bob and Janis Fleet for
planning this wonderful event. The highlight of the banquet
was the presentation of the Eagle badge to Eli Fleet. Eli
certainly has set a wonderful example that all our future Boy
Scouts can aspire to.
Our hats are off to all the parents who either served as
den leaders or assisted at our monthly Pack meetings and our
outings. Without you, none of the wonderful activities would
have been possible. Special thanks go to my wife, Deena,
who served both as a den assistant and support for me in my
8th year as Cubmaster.
The 5th grade Webelos den was led this year by Alyssa
Vining and Stacy Epstein. Our older scouts successfully
earned their Arrow of Light Award and “bridged” over to Boy
Scouts. We look forward to seeing them involved in Scouting
for many more years.
Jeri Schwartz and Deena Richman led an energetic
4th grade Weblos den. These boys went on a variety of field
trips and worked very hard to earn their Webelos Badge.
The future Webelos of the 3rd grade were led by Alyssa
Vining and Missy Frisch, this past year. Double thanks to
Alyssa for her double duty!!! These boys had a variety of
activities which led to their earning the Bear badge along with
many gold and silver arrows.
The 2nd grade Cubs were led by first year leader Kim
Gartner and by Stacy Epstein. These den leaders did a terrific
job with a huge group of boys in their first year of Scouting.
Kim and Stacy kept the weekly meetings interesting, and we
are indebted to them for their efforts. These boys earned their
Wolf badges and had a wonderful and educational experience.
Our increase in members this year was due in part to
our very first Kindergarten Tiger Cub den. GO TIGER
CUBS!!!!! Although each parent was an awesome coach, two
sets of parents stood out as leaders. They were Bruce and
Cathy Stark and Bob and Sherril Kent. They did an
unbelievable job, as we learned together about the exciting
world of Tiger Cubs. Our wonderful and enthusiastic Tigers
graduated into Cub Scouts.

Scouting
Boy Scout Troop 14
Troop 14 celebrated its 80th anniversary by continuing
the scouting tradition at the Jacksonville Jewish Center with
another year of outdoor fun, adventure and activities in 1998
-99. Bob Fleet served as Scoutmaster, aided by Assistant
Scoutmasters Louis Schwartz and Billy Wilensky. Youth
leadership was provided by Eli Fleet, Junior Assistant
Scoutmaster, Justin Jackrel, Senior Patrol Leader, and Jared
Fleet, Assistant Senior Patrol Leader.
This year, the troop participated in the River Bend
District Camporee at Echokotee. The scouts also camped at
Oleno State Park and at Kings Bay Naval Base, where they
toured a Trident submarine. On a boat trip to Nassau Sound,
they also enjoyed tubing and jet skiing. Other activities ranged
from participating in a Food Bank project to playing miniature
golf.
Thanks to the leadership efforts of Eagle Scout Sol
Proctor, funds were raised to purchase a trailer for troop gear.
The trailor was put to use right away, hauling gear to summer
camp at Camp Daniel Boone in North Carolina.
If you enjoy
camping, sports and other
outdoor activities, and are
between the ages of 11 and
18, join us at our
meetings on Thursday
nights at the Center. We
also welcome volunteer
assistance from adults.
For more information,
call Bob Fleet at 268-2746 (home) or 730-8103 (work).
Scouts on a white water rafting trip.
Troop 14 looks forward to continuing the tradition of
providing Jewish youth with a Boy Scout experience, as we
enter the new millenium.
Many scouts made advancements this year. Seven boys
completed the requirements for the Ner Tamid award.
The theme of this year’s Blue and Gold Banquet was
“80 Years of Scouting—80 Years of Eagles”, commemorating
this special anniversary. Eagle Scouts, who were former
members of Troop 14, were invited to participate in the Eagle
Court of Honor for Eli Fleet, who became the 56th Eagle
Scout from this troop. Brian Sexton, the voice of the Jaguars
and an Eagle Scout, himself, was the guest speaker.
Back from camp with the troop’s new trailer.
Scouts receiving certificates of completion
of Ner Tamid, with counselor Robin Morris.
New Eagle Scout, Eli Fleet, with Blue &
Gold Banquet speaker, Brian Sexton.

Recreation
Center Day Camp — The Place to Be!
The Center Day Camp programs were out of this world. In addition to the traditional,
fun activities like swimming, arts and crafts, and Judaica, our campers rode horses, went
boating, and even met a Bengal tiger!
A helicopter from Jax NAS landed on our field to celebrate the 4th of July with us.
Our Drama Camp sang patriotic songs and waved flags to welcome our guests.
Camp Yom Tov went bowling, played laser tag, roller skated and splashed around
Wet N’ Wild.
Camp K’ton had weekly themes for their
activities: “A Camping We Will Go.”, “Old
MacDonald’s Farm”, “Celebrate the Century”, “Outer
Space Place”, “Ocean Fun”, “Wacky Zoo Animals”.
“Under the Big Top Festival” and “Tropical Fantasy”.
A highlight was learning about fish at Fisherman’s Dock
and then about learning goy taku, the ancient Japanese
""art of fish painting.
Judaica Camp collected food for JFCS, visited
the sick and learned about kashrut and kosher symbols.
A variety of great Specialty Camps included: Basketball, Judaica-on-Wheels,
Computers, Drama, Baseball, Arts & Crafts, Sports, Cheerleading and Golf.
Evening ‘lock-ins”, color war and the annual Camp Carnival were a big hit. Parents
and campers enjoyed the booths, games, prizes, food and raffle at the Carnival.
CIT’s had leadership and first aid training, fun trips and wonderful bonding
experiences.
Many thanks to everyone who made this
summer’s camp such a big success, including: Lisa Wolfson, Hannah Bendit, Edith
Horovitz, Dodi Kress, Sharon Seebol, Adria Krantz, Billy Wilson, Gayle Bailys,
Frances Loncle, all the volunteers and the Center Maintenance Department. See
you next summer!
— Laura Cagan, Camp K’ton Director
Mike Schultz, Camp Yom Tov Director
Pam Maman, CIT Coordinator

Sunday Sports - Basketball Program
The Sunday Sports Association (SS A) provides area youth with alternative athletic
programs on Sunday afternoons. All the games and practices are held in the Fletcher-
Selber Auditorium of the Jacksonville Jewish Center. Thank you to Gayle Bailys who
coordinated a very successful program and to the volunteer coaches for their valuable
assistance and time. We look forward to an exciting 1999-2000 season.

Community Agencies
Jacksonville Jewish Federation
8505 San Jose Blvd. Jacksonville, FL 32217
448-5000 Fax.- 448-5715
The Jacksonville Jewish Federation
serves as a central resource for our Jewish
community. In summary, the Federation
is dedicated to providing for the welfare
of every Jewish person living in
Jacksonville. Through a partnership with
the United Jewish Communities, formerly
known as UJA, we are equally committed
to the survival of, and quality of life for,
every Jew living in Israel and throughout
the Diaspora.
The four major local recipient
agencies of funds raised by the Federation
are the Jewish Community Alliance,
Jewish Family & Community Services,
River Garden Hebrew Home and the
Jacksonville Jewish Foundation. We are
proud of the invaluable services provided
by these four outstanding Jewish agencies.
It is a privilege to assist them in trying to
meet their goals.
Jewish education is extremely
important, and the Federation is proud to
support the Solomon Schechter Day
School, Beit Midrash and Etz Chaim
Hebrew Academy. Through the Joan Levin
Gift of Israel program, Federation is helping
to make the dream of a trip to Israel a reality
for Jewish teens in our community.
The Federation is involved with
community relations, leadership development
and Missions to Israel. We will continue to
work in cooperation with our local agencies,
UJC and the synagogues to address the vital
issues and challenges in the entire arena of
Jewish continuity.
Our Board wishes the members of the
Jacksonville Jewish Center a Happy &
Healthy New Year.
As this yearbook is dedicated to
Rabbi Dov Kentof, we wish to join with the
many members of our Jewish community,
who understand Dov’s commitment to the
Jewish education of our young people, in
saying Mazel Tov to him and his family.
— Scot N. Ackerman, M.D., President
Alan Margolies, Executive Director

Jacksonville Jewish Foundation
4131 Sunbeam Road, Suite 275
Jacksonville, Florida 32257
Phone: 394-0720 • Fax: 394-0956
The Jacksonville Jewish Foundation is dedicated to accumulating permanent
assets which can provide a source of income to help support the stability and
continuity of the Agencies and Synagogues in Jacksonville. The Foundation
professionally administers lifetime and testamentary giving plans designed to:
• Assist individuals to achieve their personal charitable goals in the most tax-
advantaged manner.
• Accumulate enduring endowed resources for use in supporting special,
emergency, and future needs, including those not provided for by the Jacksonville
Jewish Federation’s annual campaign.
The Foundation exists as a partnership of Jacksonville’s Synagogues and
Agencies to assure a better future for all generations. Through the Foundation, donors
are provided with many ways to perpetuate their charitable interests through a wide
array of funding opportunities.
The Jacksonville Jewish Foundation congratulates Rabbi Dov Kentof for
his splendid work and dedication for the past 20 years.

Past Board Presidents
The JCA continues to grow and change, to strengthen our Jewish commitment and
Jewish involvement. We also continue to make improvements to our building, equipment,
programs, services, and staff.
Our identity is important. From the moment you enter the JCA, you are met with
positive affirmation of Jewish culture and heritage. Jewish music and videos are played
continuously in the lobby. The lobby is decorated for each Jewish holiday as part of our
celebration, and as a way of introducing some to, and rekindling others with, the important
cycle of events in the Jewish year. There is a “hamisha” feeling, as we serve people of all
ages — from 6 week old babies to senior adults.
The mission of the JCA is to (1) contribute to the continuation of Jewish life, culture,
and community, (2) provide a common meeting ground for the Jewish community, (3)
enhance the quality of life for all segments of the community, and (4) strengthen family
life. The JCA fulfills its mission through an integrated range of high quality programs for
people of all ages including: child care and family programs; fitness and recreational
facilities and activities; Jewish education, culture and arts programs; and by providing a
place for family, “neighborhood,” and community gatherings.
It is with great pride that we are able to work with the Jacksonville Jewish Center
and other Jacksonville synagogues and agencies in conducting special educational
programs and holiday celebrations.
The JCA was freed of its mortgage debt this year thanks to a group of visionary
leaders. We now move into the next century to continue our mission of service to the
Jewish Community and all our members. A sliding fee scale is available to make
membership affordable to all. We invite you to be a part of the JCA — after all — YOU
ALREADY BELONG. Shalom!
River Garden Auxiliary
The River Garden Auxiliary is unique. It began in 1922 with a small
group of ladies who called themselves the Ladies Hebrew Home Sheltering
Aid Society. The Group was formed to help care for the 12 residents in the
house on Riverside Ave. Today our goals remain the same, to enhance the
daily lives of each and every resident.
As volunteers, we care for our own and any one else who needs our
tender loving care. The Auxiliary has so many examples of caring people
serving the needs of our residents, caring unselfishly and with great tenderness.
Auxiliary volunteers give of their time willingly and with love, a fact of which
we are so proud. The Auxiliary also gives financial support for ancillary
needs and services for the residents.
Caring and Sharing, the perfect way to bring happiness and joy into
someone’s day. As part of the Auxiliary, you can make a difference.
— Gayle D. Bailys, Auxiliary President

Community Agencies
River (ffijpa) Garden
HEBREW HOME/WOLFSON HEALTH & AGING CENTER
11401 Old St. Augustine Road • 260-9020 • www.rivergarden.org
“Eldercare At Its Best”
“Honor thy father and mother that thy days may be long . . .” It was this
commandment which inspired the founding of River Garden Hebrew Home in
1946. It was this commandment which nourished the love and care that for more
than fifty years has made River Garden a nationally recognized model of
excellence in its field. It was this commandment that made it necessary to create
a Home that is welcoming to families and encourages its use as an extension of
family space. River Garden residents are a part of the community, not apart from it!
The River Garden Hebrew Home has also become the anchor of a growing
system of elder services including the Home, The Coves, Family Care Support
program and Home Health Agency. The success of River Garden is based on the
tradition of meeting 100 percent of local Jewish community needs and of serving
rich and poor alike with excellence. The River Garden Foundation accepts
donations to help River Garden continue to meet its mission. This would not be
possible without substantial charitable support from the community and the work
of The River Garden Foundation to stimulate planned gift annuities, trusts and
bequests.
River Garden’s programs of short-term rehabilitative/respite care, long¬
term residential care, Alzheimers’ and Adult Day Care, serve over 180 people
on any given day. These programs are guided by a devoted, professional full
time staff of over 200. Staff includes physicians and beauticians; nurses, social
workers, pharmacists, activities specialists; physical occupational and speech
therapists; dieticians, etc. In addition, scores of dedicated volunteers help create
a special caring community.
Located on a 35 acre Mandarin campus containing lush Florida oak and
pine trees, a private lake, meandering walking paths, River Garden is the perfect
setting for residents and visitors. River Garden is a community where people
live, love and care; a community of many lifestyles and of rich Jewish content,
and a community which every day strives to live up to the mandate of the Fifth
Commandment.
In recent years, life on campus has become more active and attractive with
the completion of The Coves, the elegant, affordable retirement community.

The River Garden Foundation is a philanthropic organization, established
to provide resources for programs and facilities to enhance the quality of life for
the aged. Its primary purpose is to fund the not-for-profit River Garden system of
services.
The foundation is dedicated to helping the elderly remain in control of their
own lives by assuring services to people at all levels of need and financial ability.
The aim of the Foundation is to keep pace with the changing needs of the
aging through programs that meet a broad array of health care needs, as well as
provide a full spectrum of residential options.

Community Agencies
Jewish Family & Community Services
3601 Cardinal Point Drive
Jacksonville, FL 32257-5582 • Phone 448-1933
Iris T. Young, Executive Director
Jewish Family & Community Services strives to be pro-active in meeting the
needs of the Jewish community. The agency is both visionary and responsive.
Adoption
JFCS continues to place babies into loving homes across the country. The decision
to adopt is highly personal, and the agency treats adoptive parents and birthparents
with respect and consideration.
Bus Rental
If you’re facing the daunting challenge of shuttling guests and family to and from life
cycle events and family gatherings, remember that the JFCS buses are available to rent.
Catering Service
Need a caterer for brunches, engagement parties, bar and bat mitzvahs and other
life cycle events? JFCS will provide delicious food, tastefully presented, while
observing dietary laws.
Community Kosher Nutrition Program
CKNP continues to provide hot, delicious, kosher meals to the seniors in our community.
The program creates a friendly, social environment centered around nutrition.
Counseling
JFCS may be best known for its quality mental health services. A staff of caring,
qualified professionals works with individuals, couples, families and children.
Services include pre-marital counseling, divorce mediation, custody home studies,
grief counseling and family counseling. Confidentiality is always guaranteed, and
most insurance plans are accepted.
Feed A Needy Neighbor
Thanks to donations of cash and non-perishable food items from a concerned
community, JFCS provides emergency groceries to families and individuals
experiencing difficult times.
Planned Lifetime Assistance Network
PLAN enables individuals to arrange for the future care of themselves or their
loved ones. Children of aging parents or relatives of disabled individuals can contract
with JFCS to ensure that the financial and social needs of these individuals are
taken care of throughout the course of their lives.
Senior Transportation
JFCS still transports seniors to religious services, medical appointments, shopping
centers and recreational activities for a very affordable fee. The Shalom Shuttle
and Mitzvah Mobile are air-conditioned, handicap-accessible buses operated by
courteous, professional drivers who provide door-to-door service.
Support Groups
Sometimes the best way to tackle a problem is to talk with others facing the same
situation. JFCS offers a variety of support groups, ranging from Age Spot for adult
children of aging parents to Camp Whatchamacallit for adopted and foster kids.

Community Organizations
American Red Magen David for Israel
Founded in 1930 as a First Aid Society, Magen David
Adorn has become the State of Israel’s emergency medical,
disaster, ambulance and healthcare network. 365 days a year,
24 hours a day, every person in every corner of Israel looks to
Magen David Adorn to perform the usual tasks carried out by
Red Cross Societies throughout the world. Within minutes,
MDA's rescue units arrive on the scene for medical
emergencies, accidents and, unfortunately, terrorist bombings.
Trained paramedics administer immediate help, and then
transport the patient to the hospital if necessary.
Mitzvah Chapter’s Annual Raffle proceeds help support
the Emanuel Celler First Aid Station in Haifa.
Even though the symbol of Magen David Adorn, a red
Star of David, is recognized by the American Red Cross,
efforts are still going on to achieve international acceptance
of our symbol.
As part of our continuing efforts to raise every possible
dollar, we have arranged for anyone who can, to donate their
car, van, motorhome or boat—running or not!—to benefit
ARMDI. Its fully tax deductible. Call (800) 550-3333 and
mention ARMDI for details and/or pickup.
You can show your support for the State of Israel for
only $18 (chai - life), and do the mitzvah of pikkuach nefesh
- saving a soul, by joining today. “For us it’s only a check, for
them it could mean life itself.”

Brandéis University
National Women’s Committee
The mission of the Brandéis University National
Women’s Committee is to provide financial support and
growth for the Brandéis University Libraries, which serve a
community of students and scholars, in education and
research, united by their commitment to the pursuit of
knowledge. The National Women’s Committee offers its
members opportunity for intellectual pursuit, continuing
education, community service, social interaction, personal
enrichment, and leadership development. The members act
as emissaries to support and enhance the image of Brandéis,
a Jewish-sponsored, non-sectarian university where
excellence is the tradition.
For more information, call Norma Levy, 273-1575.

Hadassah
National Council of Jewish Women
“Hadassah has always been an important bridge to peace.
By treating all people without regard to nationality or religion—
Hadassah has shown the world what peace in the Middle East
will look like.” -Yitzchak Rabin, Jerusalem, 1994.
Judaism teaches that it is not enough to avoid iniquity —
we must actively pursue righteousness and justice at home, in
the, community, and in the world. In this tradition, Hadassah
was founded in 1912 by Henrietta Szold to bring public health
services to pre-state Israel. Today, more than 300,000 American
women support our network of Israel projects in addition to
our volunteer work at home. Across the US, Hadassah promotes
health education, community service, and Jewish education and
research. Hadassah advocates on issues ranging from Israel-
US relations to First Amendment protections to women’s rights
and health concerns.
One by one, we must each take responsibility for
transforming hopes, promises, and echoes into deeds.
Jacksonville Hadassah invites your participation in one of our
four groups: Hannah Senesch, Shir Li, Tikva, and Nurse’s
Council.
For information please contact any of our presidents:
Chapter Phyllis Goldberg and Robin Morris
Hannah Senesch Esther Glasser and Mozella Hayes
Shir Li Robin Allerding
Tikva contact Janis Dorman
Jacksonville Chapter of Hadassah Board:
The National Council of Jewish Women (NCJW)-
Jacksonville Section, Inc. is a volunteer organization, inspired
by Jewish values, that works through a program of research,
education, advocacy, and community service to improve the
quality of life for women, children and families, and strives to
ensure individual rights and freedoms for all.
The Jacksonville section was established in 1939, and
has been involved in the following programs:
• Tutoring “at risk” girls at PACE to provide them with a
second chance to earn a diploma and job skills;
• Bringing kosher meals, as well as a caring word, to the
homebound (Kosher Kart);
• Starting a model program, later adopted nationwide, to
provide abused children with a voice in the court system
(Guardian Ad Litem);
• Bringing the Home Instructional Program for Preschool
Youngsters (HIPPY), a school-readiness program for at risk
4 and 5 year olds to Jacksonville;
• Spearheading advocacy efforts at the local, state, and
national levels for programs and policies which impact our
six priority areas, which include women’s issues, children
and youth, health and aging, constitutional rights, Jewish
Life, and Israel;
• Provide educational monthly programs to educate the
community about a variety of topics.
For information, contact Ellen Rubens —737-1552 or
the NCJW Action Line — 443-2820
